He performs the morning routine — shave, knot the tie, look at his own face in the mirror without quite looking at it — as a kind of armoring. The smallest disruption (a child's noise, a wife's voice raised in cheerfulness, eggs cooked the wrong way) registers as an assault and is filed but not acted on. He leaves the house clenched.

**Workday — best functional window.** The lab and the calculations occupy enough working memory to crowd out the persecutory ideation. Colleagues see a quiet, capable, slightly grim man. He produces. The performance of competence soothes the narcissistic overlay temporarily. This is the closest he comes to relief.

**Evening transition — the dangerous hour.** The drive home is when the protective structure begins to give. The closer he gets to the house, the more accessible the core self-image becomes. By the time he is in the driveway the contamination narrative is back online. He enters the house already loaded for the projective work.

**First drinks — false ease, then disinhibition.** The first two or three drinks produce the only experience of relaxation he is capable of having. Rebecca, in the early years, learned to read this window as a brief safety. The next several drinks dismantle the public-self compartmentalization. The face-mask comes off. Verbal aggression begins — sarcasm aimed at Bruce's precocity, contempt aimed at Rebecca's tenderness, monologues about contamination and inheritance delivered with the false-rational cadence of a man who believes he is teaching.

**Late evening — discharge.** Verbal escalates to physical. The target selection is governed by safety: the smaller body first if both are present, the wife when the wife intervenes, the wife alone when the child has been hidden or sent to bed. The violence is not random; it is the *daily evacuation* of the day's accumulated unbearable interior, dumped through the only outlet he has built.

**Sleep — false reset.** He sleeps it off. He does not, in the morning, fully remember or fully not-remember; he occupies a productive amnesia where the events are present enough to feel justified by ("look what you made me do") and absent enough to deny if challenged. The cycle resumes.

This is the *small* decompensation. It runs nightly. It is the metronome under everything else.

---

## 3. The Larger Decompensation Arc

Superimposed on the daily cycle is a slower, multi-year deterioration with discrete phase transitions. The published record sketches at least four such phases.

**Phase I — Pre-Bruce. Latent.** Married, employed, drinking, beating Rebecca on a developing but not yet fully crystallized schedule. The contamination ideation is present but pre-acted; the sterilization attempt occurs in this phase as a *prophylactic* against the next phase. He is trying, in his own warped grammar, to prevent his own decompensation by preventing the stimulus he knows he cannot survive: a child of his own to project onto. The attempt fails. The stimulus arrives.

**Phase II — Infant/early-childhood Bruce. Crystallization.** The delusional system locks onto its object. From the moment of Bruce's existence the projection has somewhere to land. The phase is paradoxically *stabilizing* for Brian — having a container reduces some of the formless dread — at the cost of catastrophic destabilization for the household. This is the phase of routinized child-directed cruelty: the cold staring at the crib, the refusal to hold, the reading of every developmental milestone as evidence of monstrosity, the early physical roughness disguised as discipline.

**Phase III — Bruce's intellectual emergence and Rebecca's protective coalescence. Acute destabilization.** Bruce begins reading early, doing arithmetic young, displaying the gift that will eventually define him. Rebecca, recognizing both her son's brilliance and her husband's mounting danger to it, draws closer to the child. Two pressure points fire simultaneously: the narcissistic injury (the son outshines the father) and the abandonment terror (the wife allies with the disowned self). Brian's daily cycle now runs hotter; the violence escalates in both frequency and severity; the contamination monologues lengthen; the drinking deepens. This is the phase of greatest household terror and the phase during which the homicide becomes statistically inevitable.

**Phase IV — The exit attempt and the homicide. Catastrophic discharge.** Rebecca decides to leave with Bruce. This is, per the empirical literature on intimate-partner homicide as well as the textual record, the lethal moment. Brian's defensive architecture cannot survive her exit — it would force him to see what she is fleeing, and what she is fleeing is what he has spent a lifetime not-seeing about himself. He intercepts. He kills. The killing is committed in front of the child not by accident but because the child is the original container of the projection: the audience the killing requires. After the act, the public-self compartmentalization re-asserts with terrifying speed — he coaches, he threatens, he beats the case. This is decompensation followed by hyper-recompensation under legal stakes: the system can still find the suit when the suit is required for survival.

**Phase V — Institutionalization. Forced exterior structure.** Stripped of alcohol, stripped of the household, stripped of the projective object, supplied with rules and walls and observers, he stabilizes in the brittle institutional way that personality-disordered patients often do — well-behaved, articulate, capable of the right answers in clinical interviews, mistaken for improved. Inside, the structure is untouched. He is biding.

**Phase VI — Release and the graveside. Terminal relapse.** Out of the institution, the decompensation resumes on contact with stimuli, because nothing has been resolved — only paused. He seeks out Bruce. He goes to the grave. The choice of venue is itself diagnostic: the grave is Rebecca, is the evidence of what he did, is the original scene re-staged for the original audience. He cannot stay away from it because the projective structure requires its containers and both are there. He attacks. He dies. The system breaks against the son who has, by now, grown larger than him.

---

## 4. The Specific Triggers and Their Specific Decompensations

Different stressors break different seams. Granular map:

**Trigger: Bruce displays intelligence.** Decompensation pathway: narcissistic injury → instant cognitive narrowing onto the monster-narrative ("only a *thing* would read like that") → verbal humiliation of the child (mockery of the book, the equation, the question asked) → if the wife defends, escalation to physical. Latency from trigger to violence: minutes to hours, depending on alcohol load.

**Trigger: Rebecca shows physical affection to Bruce.** Decompensation pathway: abandonment-terror activated → splitting of Rebecca into betraying-mother representation → cold withdrawal first (the silent dinner), then sarcastic verbal aggression, then physical aggression toward Rebecca later that night, frequently in the bedroom out of the child's sight. Latency: hours; the violence is often delayed and "saved" for the private hour. This is one of the few patterns in which his impulse control is relatively *better* — because the satisfaction depends on Rebecca knowing what she is being punished for, and that requires staging.

**Trigger: Workplace humiliation or perceived professional slight.** Decompensation pathway: he cannot discharge at work; the suppression cost is high; he arrives home pre-loaded; the first available domestic stimulus serves as pretext for a discharge whose true source is the lab. Latency: same-day, evening. The wife and child have no way to know what they are being punished for; the violence appears, to them, random — which is the worst kind, because it cannot be predicted or avoided.

**Trigger: Sobriety, enforced or attempted.** Decompensation pathway: without the gate-valve, the persecutory interior floods upward in waking hours. He becomes agitated, paces, talks more about contamination, sleeps poorly, and either resumes drinking quickly or moves to physical violence earlier in the evening. Sobriety does not improve him; it accelerates him. This is why institutional stays appear to "work" only inside the institution.

**Trigger: A mirror to his own father.** Any moment — a phrase he hears himself say that was his father's, a posture he catches in a window, Bruce flinching in a way Brian once flinched — that threatens to surface the identification-with-the-aggressor. Decompensation pathway: instantaneous, defensive rage. The recognition cannot be allowed to land; the violence is dispatched specifically to drown it. These are the most dangerous incidents because they are the most affectively saturated and the least cognitively mediated.

**Trigger: Imminent loss / abandonment.** Decompensation pathway: total collapse of the compartmentalization, full surfacing of the core monster-self, lethal violence. This is the seam along which he ultimately commits homicide.

**Trigger: Direct confrontation about the abuse.** Never observed during Rebecca's life because she did not survive long enough to escalate to it. Implicit, however, in the graveside encounter: when the adult Bruce stands in front of him as evidence and accuser, the decompensation is immediate and physical. He attacks rather than answer.

---

## 5. The Shape of Collapse

When Brian Banner breaks fully — as opposed to discharging on the daily schedule — the collapse has a recognizable morphology.

**Cognitive features.** Profound narrowing of attention onto the persecutory content. The contamination/monster narrative becomes the only available frame; alternative interpretations of events are inaccessible. Time-sense compresses to the present incident. Capacity for consequentialist reasoning (what happens if I do this) drops sharply — visible in the parking-lot homicide, committed in public view.

**Affective features.** A specific quality of *hot* rage layered over older, deeper terror and shame. The rage is recruited precisely because the terror and shame are unbearable; the rage is doing the work of not-feeling them. Observers describe the eyes as both fixed and somehow elsewhere — looking at the wife, seeing the father, the self, the monster, the contamination, the whole evacuative project at once.

**Somatic features.** Tachycardia, sweating, the flush of the face, dilation of pupils, fine tremor of the hands which steadies the moment a weapon (a fist, a bottle, eventually nothing more than a stretch of asphalt) is acquired. The motor system smooths under violence; this is the discharge he was built for, and the body recognizes it.

**Verbal features.** Repetition. The same phrases recur across decompensations because they are not communications but incantations — "look what you made me do," "you're not human," "I knew it," "I told her," "this is what you are." The vocabulary shrinks. The cadence is his father's cadence, though he does not hear it as such.

**Behavioral features.** Pursuit. He follows. He does not let a stimulus leave a room without him; the abandonment-terror trigger especially produces relentless tracking behavior — through the house, out the door, into the parking lot, into the cemetery years later. The pursuit pattern is one of the most stable signatures across his entire violent record.

**Post-incident features.** Rapid re-compartmentalization. Within minutes of a discharge he can be sitting in a chair again, drink in hand, demanding dinner, watching the news, behaving as if the household has not just been wrecked. This is not amnesia; it is the active reinstallation of the public-self overlay. The speed of this re-installation is one of the most chilling features of the file and is itself diagnostic — it implies that the violent state is *ego-syntonic* in the moment and is filed afterward as having been *justified*, not aberrant.

---

## 6. What Does *Not* Produce Decompensation

Equally instructive — the negative space.

He does not decompensate under ordinary professional stress. He absorbs it.

He does not decompensate under physical illness, injury, or pain. He absorbs those too; the man raised under his father's hand has a high physical-pain tolerance and treats his own body, like Bruce's, as a thing to be punished and used.

He does not decompensate under social embarrassment outside the home. He absorbs that and brings it home.

He does not decompensate, importantly, into *despair*. There is no depicted suicidal collapse, no period of immobilizing depression, no breakdown into help-seeking. The personality structure forecloses the route by which a man might fall *inward*. All his collapse vectors point outward, at others. This is one of the deepest features of the case and one of its grimmest: the absence of any internal channel for the unbearable affect means there is no safety valve except other people's bodies.

---

## 7. The Conditions That Would Have Produced True Collapse

Speculative but evidence-grounded. The events that *would have* broken him in a different, non-violent direction — that would have forced the structure to fail inward rather than outward — are precisely the events the structure was built to prevent.

- Sustained sobriety in a containing therapeutic relationship with a clinician who could tolerate his hostility without retaliating or abandoning. This was never offered; the institutional stay appears to have been custodial.
- A confrontation with his own father, surviving and undeniable, that forced the identification into consciousness.
- The death of Bruce while still a child — which would have removed the projective container and left the disowned self with nowhere to go. Most likely outcome: acute psychotic decompensation, possibly suicide. (He was, in a real sense, protected from his own deepest collapse by his son's survival; one of the bitter ironies of the file.)
- Late-life cognitive decline that eroded the compartmentalization machinery. He did not live to it.

The actual terminal collapse — the graveside death — is the structure's last and most characteristic failure: he died still attacking, still pursuing, still discharging outward, never once having turned to look at what was inside him. The headstone that killed him bore his wife's name. The geometry of the death is the geometry of the whole life: he ran at the evidence of what he had done and broke himself against it without ever seeing it.

That is the final decompensation. He did not break down. He broke *forward*, into the stone, and stopped.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT: BRIAN BANNER

## Preliminary Note on the Frame

The subject is deceased — killed circa Bruce Banner's late adolescence in the headstone altercation at Rebecca's grave. A conventional forward assessment is therefore moot in the biological register. But this dossier treats Brian Banner as a *system input still running* — a posthumous variable continuing to act on the world through (a) the introjected paternal voice inside Bruce's psychic architecture, (b) the cosmological reframings later writers have laid over the Banner household, and (c) the live possibility of canonical resurrection, dream-return, alternate-timeline iteration, and metaphysical re-emergence that the Hulk corpus has demonstrated it will use. The forward assessment therefore proceeds along four tracks: the counterfactual (had he lived), the introjected (the live Brian inside Bruce), the metaphysical (Brian as cosmological actor in the Ewing-era frame and its successors), and the editorial (the recurring narrative pressures that keep dragging him back to the page).

---

## 1. The Counterfactual Trajectory — Had The Headstone Missed

Reconstructing the life Brian would have lived had the graveside altercation ended with bruises rather than death is not idle speculation; it disciplines the assessment by forcing the question of *what he was capable of becoming*. The honest answer, on the evidence, is: nothing better.

**The five-year window post-institutionalization.** Brian was discharged from the psychiatric facility without — by every indication in canon — substantive insight. The contamination delusion was not extinguished; it was waiting. His first volitional act on regaining access to Bruce was to seek him out and physically attack him. This is the diagnostically decisive datum. A man who has done years of containment-and-medication-only psychiatric time, who emerges and immediately re-stages the original violence on the now-grown evidence of his "monstrous" progeny, has not been treated; he has been paused. The probability of any spontaneous remission in the five years after discharge approaches zero. The pattern observed in batterers with delusional encapsulation and severe AUD who survive the index homicide is recidivism toward intimate violence within months of regained access.

**Likely next targets.** Bruce, primarily — he would have continued to seek the son out, alternating intimidation visits with periods of withdrawal. Any subsequent romantic partner of Brian's own would have been at acute lethality risk; the Rebecca homicide was a successfully-rehearsed solution to the abandonment dynamic, and rehearsed solutions repeat. There is no evidence in the record of any post-Rebecca relationship, but a man of his presentability and credentialing would have re-partnered; the woman who took him on would have inherited the unresolved structure.

**Occupational arc.** The institutionalization would have ended the security clearance and almost certainly the Los Alamos / ordnance-adjacent career. Likely landing places: adjunct teaching at a second-tier institution; private-sector contracting at the technical periphery; a slow professional declension that would itself have functioned as a fresh narcissistic injury feeding the cycle. The intelligence was real but it required institutional scaffolding to express; absent that scaffolding, with the AUD untreated, the cognitive decline curve steepens. By his mid-sixties one would expect frank alcohol-related cognitive impairment overlaid on the personality structure — a dementing antisocial, which is the worst kind to manage clinically because the disinhibition rises while the residual social monitoring falls.

**Terminal trajectory in the counterfactual.** Three modal endpoints, in descending probability: (1) a second homicide, most likely of a subsequent partner, ending in incarceration or re-institutionalization; (2) a suicide, more probable in a late-career collapse scenario when the compensatory grandiose self can no longer be maintained — the contamination delusion turned inward terminally; (3) a slow medical death from cirrhosis or alcohol-related cardiomyopathy in his sixties, alone, in degraded housing, the file closing with a county coroner's report.

What is essentially *not* on the probability distribution: any form of repair with Bruce, any meaningful sobriety, any retrospective acknowledgment of Rebecca's murder as murder. The defensive structure is not equipped to metabolize those acknowledgments; they would dismantle the self.

---

## 2. The Introjected Brian — Forward Assessment of the Live Persecutor Inside Bruce

This is where the forward assessment has actual ongoing stakes, because this Brian is not dead. He is the most reliably recurring antagonist in the Banner inner cosmography, more durable than any external villain.

**Current state of the introject (post-*Immortal Hulk*-era).** Bruce has, across the long arc, made successive partial peaces with the paternal introject — the Doc Samson lancing of the repressed killing; the Pantheon-era integrations; the "guilt Hulk" confrontations; the green-door cosmology of the Ewing run in which the father is rewritten as the originating mortal aperture for the One Below All's leakage into the Banner home. Each integration has been real and each has been partial. The introject has not been extinguished; it has been moved deeper, re-bordered, reframed, given different names. The structural pattern across forty years of story is *displacement, not dissolution*: the persecutory voice migrates from foreground (the literal father in flashback) to mezzanine (Guilt Hulk) to deep substrate (Devil Hulk in its persecutory guise) to cosmological (the green door). Each migration accompanies an apparent victory and a real loss of access — the deeper it goes, the harder it is to address therapeutically.

**Likely future activations.** The introjected Brian reliably re-fronts under four conditions, all of which are recurrent in Bruce's life:

1. **Fatherhood threats** — actual or potential procreation, custody questions, the appearance of a Banner child (Skaar, the alternate-timeline children, any future iteration). Each of these activates the contamination/monster-progeny script Brian deposited. Future paternity stories will, by structural necessity, summon Brian.
2. **Intimate partnership stabilization** — paradoxically, periods of relative happiness with a partner (Betty, or any successor) reliably summon the introject, because the structure cannot tolerate the disconfirmation of Brian's worldview that domestic peace represents.
3. **Recognition of his own violence as paternal in origin** — any episode in which Bruce as Hulk does harm that he must integrate as *his*, not as an externalized other's, calls up the original author of the pattern.
4. **Loss-of-control events under intoxicants, illness, or possession** — the Brian voice is the voice of the disinhibited self, and any condition that mimics intoxication or dissociation will give it the mic.

**Fork point: the integration that has never happened.** The one therapeutic move not yet executed in canon, and the one that would constitute the genuine forward growth vector, is *grief for Brian*. Not forgiveness — forgiveness is the false fork, frequently dangled, never appropriate. *Grief* — the mourning of the father Brian was not and never could have been, the acknowledgment that the man was himself a child beaten into a monster, without collapsing that acknowledgment into exculpation. This is the move that would convert the introjected persecutor into an integrated, sorrowful ancestor — a dead man who can be carried rather than a live voice that must be fought. Doc Samson got partway there in #s 376–377 by surfacing the killing; he did not get to the mourning. Until the mourning is done the introject keeps its teeth.

**Catastrophe vector for the introject.** Conversely, the worst-case forward path is *literalization* — a story in which Brian is resurrected, returned in flesh, brought back as antagonist. The corpus has shown the appetite for this (the cosmological reframings already gesture at it; the green door is the structural permission slip). A literalized Brian would re-externalize what decades of work have moved inward toward integrability, and would reset Bruce's clock. The signs to watch for: any narrative that gives Brian a "real" cosmological role independent of Bruce's psyche, any resurrection-tier event in the Hulk corner of the universe, any green-door arc that names Brian as warden rather than victim.

---

## 3. The Metaphysical Brian — Cosmological Forward Vectors

The Ewing-era reframing did something specific and durable: it elevated Brian from a domestic abuser whose damage was psychological to a *cosmologically significant* figure whose household was the mortal-plane aperture for a Below entity. This is a writerly move with consequences for forward assessment, because it converts Brian from a finite biographical fact into an open metaphysical variable.

**Open questions the cosmological frame leaves.**

- Is Brian himself, in any sense, persisting in the Below? The corpus is coy. The green door is bi-directional; things that go in can come out. The Devil Hulk's lineage of internal persecutors borrows Brian's face; whether that borrowing is metaphor or ontology is unresolved.
- If the One Below All used the Banner household as aperture, was Brian an unwitting conduit, a willing one, or — the darkest read — was the contamination delusion *correct in its register but wrong in its content*? He believed he was contaminated and the contamination would flow through him to his child. The cosmological frame retroactively grants the structure of the delusion while changing what was actually flowing.
- What is the standing of Rebecca in the same frame? She is the unaddressed counterweight; any future cosmological work on Brian must reckon with her, and the Banner corpus has historically under-developed her.

**Forward fork in the metaphysical register.** Two roads, both plausible, with very different implications.

*Road A — Brian as recurring metaphysical antagonist.* A future arc materializes Brian as a Below-aligned entity, restored, weaponized against Bruce or against a Banner descendant. This is the editorial-easy path. It is the catastrophe path for the character work. It collapses forty years of patient internalization back into a punch-up. It is also, on the trend lines of how Marvel handles its foundational trauma figures (cf. how often Magneto's parents, Wolverine's father, Daredevil's father return in some register), the *more probable* path on a long enough timeline.

*Road B — Brian as exorcised ancestor.* A future arc — possibly a *Hulk: The End*-adjacent codetta, possibly a deliberate elegiac one-shot — uses the cosmological frame to *release* Brian: a story in which Bruce, or a successor, enters the green door and finds the father not as warden but as another beaten boy, and the recognition severs the channel. This is the growth path. It requires a writer willing to refuse the punch-up. It is rarer in the corpus but not absent (the Pantheon-era integrations and certain David codas point toward it).

The fork is genuine, and which road is taken will be determined not by the character but by editorial decisions about what the Hulk franchise is for in a given decade.

---

## 4. Recurring Editorial Pressures That Will Keep Returning Brian to the Page

A surveillance file on a dead man has to track the conditions of his disinterment. Brian Banner returns whenever the following pressures coincide:

- **A new writer is establishing their thesis on Bruce.** Each major run since Mantlo has done its own Brian sequence as a credentialing move. The next major run will too.
- **A Banner child or successor is introduced or developed.** Skaar arcs activated Brian-material; any future Banner-lineage character will.
- **A "definitive" or terminal Hulk story is being attempted.** End-state stories reach for origin-state figures by structural necessity.
- **A horror-genre turn in the Hulk corner.** The Ewing run demonstrated the appetite; future horror-Hulk arcs will recruit Brian because he is the franchise's most economical embodiment of mundane evil with cosmic reach.
- **Anniversary issues, retrospectives, and "untold tale" formats.** These return to childhood. Childhood is Brian.

The forward calendar therefore reliably contains Brian-events at roughly five-to-eight-year intervals, with the modal form being a flashback or dream-sequence (low cost, high yield) and the rare form being a literalized return (high cost, high risk to the accumulated character work).

---

## 5. The Open Questions

Listed as a working investigative agenda, in descending order of analytic importance.

1. **What did Brian know about his own father's history?** The cycle is canonically asserted but never fully excavated. The grandfather Banner is the unexamined upstream node. Any forward arc that addresses him would substantially reshape the assessment by establishing whether Brian had *any* metacognitive purchase on the pattern or was wholly inside it.
2. **What were the contents of his institutional record?** Diagnosis-of-the-day, treatment refused or accepted, any documented statements about Bruce, any documented statements about Rebecca. This is the file-within-the-file that has never been opened in canon.
3. **Did he leave writings?** A working physicist with delusional encapsulation around heredity and contamination is statistically likely to have generated notebooks — pseudoscientific elaborations of the monster-progeny thesis, perhaps. The non-appearance of such documents in canon is itself a datum; their potential appearance is a fork point. A discovered Brian-notebook is one of the most powerful unused devices the corpus has in reserve.
4. **What was the precise temporal relationship between the sterilization attempt and Rebecca's conception?** Canon is impressionistic. The order matters: a sterilization attempt that failed *before* conception is one psychological event; one performed *after* learning of the pregnancy is a different and more acute one; one performed *after* Bruce's birth, as a closing-the-stable-door act, is a third.
5. **Was there ever a moment of paternal tenderness, however brief, that Bruce has repressed?** The current record is one of unrelieved hostility from infancy. This is unusual even in severe batterer profiles, and the suspicion must be entertained that a single early bonding moment exists in the substrate and has been defended against by both father and son for opposite reasons. If such a moment were ever surfaced it would be the most destabilizing single datum the file could acquire — destabilizing because it would humanize without exculpating, which is the configuration the Banner psyche has worked hardest to prevent.

---

## 6. Growth vs. Catastrophe — The Push Factors

Stated cleanly, as a decision matrix for whichever clinician, writer, or analyst inherits this file.

**Pushes toward growth (of the Bruce-system, since Brian himself is past growth):**

- Sustained therapeutic work on *grief* rather than *forgiveness* regarding the father.
- Surfacing of the grandfather node — converting Brian from origin-point to mid-stream node in a longer river.
- Refusal of any literalized return; insistence that Brian remain a psychic and historical, not a present and corporeal, fact.
- Development of Rebecca as a full subject rather than a victim-of, restoring the maternal counterweight.
- Any successful paternity by Bruce that does not reproduce the script — the empirical disconfirmation of the contamination thesis.
- Acknowledgment by Bruce of his own paternally-derived violence without collapse into self-loathing — the *I am his son and I am not him* integration.

**Pushes toward catastrophe:**

- Literal resurrection of Brian in any register — Below-aligned, dream-given-flesh, alternate-timeline variant imported as antagonist.
- A Banner descendant who *does* reproduce the script, retroactively validating the contamination delusion at the narrative level.
- A writer who treats Brian as redeemable through Brian's own action rather than through Bruce's (and Rebecca's) — the false-forgiveness arc.
- Loss of Betty or a comparable stabilizing object under conditions that mimic the Rebecca homicide — the structural restaging that would re-activate the introject at full voltage.
- Cognitive or somatic compromise of Bruce that mimics his father's late-life decline trajectory — the body itself becoming evidence for the inheritance thesis.

---

## 7. Bottom Line

Brian Banner the man is finished. Brian Banner the *variable* is not, and on the trend lines visible across the corpus he is approximately a permanent feature of the system — not because the character is rich enough to merit perpetual return, but because the wound he opened is the wound the franchise exists to examine. The forward assessment therefore reduces to a single discipline: every story that touches Brian must be evaluated on whether it moves the wound toward integration or re-opens it for spectacle. The former is rare and precious. The latter is the default and the danger. The most important sentence in the entire file is the one that has not yet been written in canon, and which the work is asymptotically approaching: *He was a beaten boy who became a beating man, and he is dead, and I am sorry for him, and I am not him.* Until Bruce can say that sentence, Brian is still in the house.

## Relationship Graph
### [[Robert Bruce Banner, PhD (Hulk)]]
- The primary victim and the primary creation. Brian saw a monster in the crib and spent his life making it true; Bruce became, eventually and tragically, what Brian said he was, which closed the causal loop and retroactively 'confirmed' the delusion.
- Failure mode: already terminal in life (Brian killed by Bruce in the gravestone struggle); posthumously, the failure mode is permanent - he persists as the introjected voice Bruce cannot fully silence, the original 'monster' the Hulk was created to fight and which the Hulk also IS.
- Leverage on Bruce: anyone who can mimic, channel, or surface Brian's voice (Nightmare, Doc Samson in excavation, hell-realm antagonists) gains direct access to the load-bearing wound. The therapeutic version (Samson) and the weaponized version (Nightmare) use the same lever in opposite directions.

### Rebecca Banner
- Wife. Sole on-page object of any depicted near-warmth (the courtship), then sole on-page object of escalating persecution, then victim of uxoricide at the curb in front of the child.
- Failure mode: realized. The marriage was the decompensating stressor; her protection of Bruce was the perceived conspiracy; her attempt to leave was the terminal trigger.
- Leverage: the memory of Rebecca is the second-most-powerful lever on Bruce (after the introject itself); anyone who invokes her mobilizes both Bruce's grief and his rage at Brian.

### Brians Father
- Off-page, implied (David, #377 dream material). The transgenerational origin - the man who installed the catastrophic self-concept Brian spent his adult life evacuating onto his own son.
- Failure mode: already failed - the abuse was transmitted forward.
- Leverage: none operationally, but explanatorily central - he is the etiology Brian never examined.

### Doc Samson
- Indirect. Samson is the analyst who excavated the buried memory of Brian's killing from Bruce's dissociative architecture (#377 and surrounding).
- Failure mode: excavation without integration risks re-traumatizing rather than resolving; Samson's interventions sometimes destabilize the very compartments they reveal.
- Leverage: Samson's work is the principal canonical 'reach' into Brian-as-introject - therapeutic access to the load-bearing object.

### Nightmare
- Posthumous instrumental relationship. Nightmare uses Brian's image as a tormenting figure in Bruce's dreamscape - weaponizes the introject.
- Failure mode: realized; this IS the weaponized form.
- Leverage: demonstrates that anyone with access to Bruce's dream/psychic realm can reach for the Brian-figure as ready-made ammunition.
